        </div><div class="casAbstract">The combination of high-capacity and long-term cyclability has always been regarded as the first priority for next generation anode materials in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  To meet these requirements, the Ag nanoparticle decorated mesoporous SnO2/NiO nanotube (m-SNT) anodes were synthesized via an electrospinning process, followed by fast ramping rate calcination and subsequent chem. redn. in this work.  The one-dimensional porous hollow structure effectively alleviates a large vol. expansion during cycling as well as provides a short lithium-ion diffusion length.  Furthermore, metallic nickel (Ni) nanoparticles converted from the NiO nanograins during the lithiation process reversibly decomp. Li2O during delithiation process, which significantly improves the reversible capacity of the m-SNT anodes.  In addn., Ag nanoparticles uniformly decorated on the m-SNT via a simple chem. redn. process significantly improve rate capability and also contribute to long-term cyclability.  The m-SNT@Ag anodes exhibited excellent cycling stability without obvious capacity fading after 500 cycles with a high capacity of 826 mAh g-1 at a high c.d. of 1000 mA g-1.  Furthermore, even at a very high c.d. of 5000 mA g-1, the charge-specific capacity remained as high as 721 mAh g-1, corresponding to 60% of its initial capacity at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpftCbU7va2ebVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljvJ2FuKZlilA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhvVymtbfO&amp;md5=3d47d11dd5fa00e0a6870f8bdd6de061</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.07.077"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ru, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A novelporous coral-like Zn<sub>0.5</sub>Ni<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> as an anode material forlithium ion batteries with excellent rate performance</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fe2O3 embedded in the nitrogen-doped carbon matrix with strong C-O-Fe oxygen-bridge bonds for enhanced sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Tianxiao; Liao, Hanxiao; Ge, Peng; Zhang, Yu; Tian, Yiqi; Hong, Wanwan; Shi, Zidan; Shao, Chunsheng; Hou, Hongshuai; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Chemistry and Physics</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">By reason of rich Na resources, Na-ion batteries have excited enormous consideration for use in the developing energy-storage stations.  And not surprisingly, the exploration of cost-effective anode materials for SIBs have been a conspicuous topic.  Herein, Fe trioxide embedded in the N-doped C matrix with strong O-bridge bonds is synthesized by using the Fe based metal org. framework as template.  The obtained composite delivers excellent electrochem. properties, such as specific capacity of 473.7 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  Besides, the reversible capacity still remains at 155.3 mA h g-1 at the high d. of 4000 mA g-1.  This remarkable Na-ion storage capability could be attributed to the incorporation of N atoms into C matrix and the strong chem. bonds between Fe trioxide and C matrix, which can restrain electrode pulverization and also retain an interparticle connection even after long cycling that could offer a good electronic conductive pathway.  This strategy for prepg. Fe trioxide possess strong interfacial interaction with N-doped C matrix can be applied to other metal phosphides and metal oxide materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqQaoRVH8x2t7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljvJ2FuKZlilA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtVOisbzL&amp;md5=b20ddce2adeb0d8949f01490b61e0e7c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1021/jz2012066"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Slater, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an attractive alternative to lithium-ion batteries that alleviate problems with lithium availability and cost.  Despite several studies of cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries involving layered oxide materials, there are few low-voltage metal oxide anodes capable of operating sodium ion reversibly at room temp.  We have synthesized amorphous titanium dioxide nanotube electrodes directly grown on current collectors without binders and additives to use as an anode for sodium-ion batteries.  We find that only amorphous large diam. nanotubes (&gt;80 nm I.D.) can support electrochem. cycling with sodium ions.  These electrodes maximize their capacity in operando and reach reversible capacity of 150 mA-h/g in 15 cycles.  We also demonstrate for the first time a full cell all-oxide sodium-ion battery using amorphous titanium dioxide nanotube anode coupled to a Na1.0Li0.2Ni0.25Mn0.75Oδ cathode at room temp. exhibiting good rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr8q2bDG7YJCbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljvJ2FuKZlilA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1ChtLbP&amp;md5=66a2a71991a01d6823c9c01024f65c74</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201700176"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mei, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Two-Dimensional Metal Oxide Nanomaterials for Next-Generation Rechargeable Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nickel nitride is synthesized by high temp. ammonolysis of nickel(ii) hexamine and tris(ethylenediamine) salts.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Molybdenum Phosphide: A Conversion-type Anode for Ultralong-Life Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Zhaodong; Hou, Hongshuai; Wang, Chao; Li, Simin; Zhang, Yun; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">High specific capacity and long cycling life of anode materials still remain major challenges in the development of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Nowadays, transition metal phosphides have been reckoned as promising anodes in view of their high theor. specific capacities, low potential for sodium storage, and superior cond.  Herein, molybdenum phosphide (MoP) nanorods wrapped with thin carbon layer have been prepd. and applied as an anode for SIBs.  By utilizing in situ X-ray diffraction technol., a conversion-type mechanism of MoP anode has been disclosed.  This kind of MoP electrode exhibits extraordinary electrochem. properties, including excellent cycling performance with a discharge capacity of 398.4 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 800 cycles, and remarkable rate capabilities, which remain 104.5 mA g-1 at 1600 mA h g-1 even after 10,000 loops.  The distinguished performances stem from synergetic merits of the morphol., structure, and mechanism of MoP.  It is expected that MoP will be a promising anode material for SIBs and this work would provide theor. basis for the scalable research and applications of MoP-based anode materials for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoc3DRJ12UzbLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljOxjsv1LaZww"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtlWnsr3N&amp;md5=42db05d069cc8ce6437cbfdfc241593d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.03.042"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Microwave-assisted one-pot synthesis of SnC2O4/graphene composite anode material for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Shaojun; Hua, Xiaoyan; Guo, Hongtao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ceramics International</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">44</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13495-13501</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CINNDH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0272-8842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Currently, SnC2O4 is considered as one of the most promising anode materials for high-energy lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) because its charge capacity is higher than that of metal oxides.  Herein, a facile microwave-assisted solvothermal method was employed to obtain SnC2O4/GO composites within only 30 min, which is time-efficient.  The amt. of SnC2O4 was increased to 95.3 wt% to improve the capacity of the composite.  Pure SnC2O4 with a high sp. surface area of 19.6 m2 g-1 without any other tin compd. was used for fabrication.  The SnC2O4/GO composite exhibited excellent electrochem. performance, with reversible discharge/charge capacity of 657/659 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.2 A g-1.  Furthermore, at high current densities of 1.0 and 2.0 A g-1, the SnC2O4/GO composite anode exhibited high reversible discharge/charge capacities of 553/552 and 418/414 mA h g-1, resp., after 200 cycles at room temp.  These improvements were likely obtained because SnC2O4 was well composited with graphene, which not only offered rapid electron transfer but also released the tension produced by the volumetric effect during repeated lithiation/delithiation.  Cyclic voltammetry (CV) was also performed to further study the electrochem. reactions of SnC2O4/GO.  The facile microwave-assisted solvothermal method used herein is considered as a highly efficient method to fabricate metal oxalate/graphene composites for use as anode materials in LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrgjOvTLSYwtrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljOxjsv1LaZww"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXotlGkt70%253D&amp;md5=1d2cc81169e0ea29d548fc390e38c6f0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.03.087"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The shape-controlled synthesis and novel lithium storage mechanism of as-prepared CuC<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub>·xH<sub>2</sub>O nanostructures</span>. <i>J. Anhyd. mixed oxalates are used as high-capacity (ca. 600 mA h g- 1) lithium storage materials, with good capacity retention after 75 cycles.  The lithium storage mechanism is complex and involves conversion reactions together with double layer charge storage and reversible reactions with the electrolyte.  The low temp. synthesis of these materials makes them attractive materials for low-cost Li-ion electrodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoKhegnLGt-DrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWfGFFp4RqCw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsFChu73K&amp;md5=b51bef85b4ccbd793df563c092d7b858</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1002/adma.200401101"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gou, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Alpha-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Nanotubes in Gas Sensor and Lithium-ion Battery Applications</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">α-Fe2O3 nanotubes in gas sensor and lithium-ion battery applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Jun; Xu, Lina; Li, Weiyang; Gou, Xinglong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

                        cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nickel oxalate dihydrate nanorods attached to reduced graphene oxide sheets as a high-capacity anode for rechargeable lithium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Oh, Hyo-Jin; Jo, Chang-Heum; Yoon, Chong Seung; Yashiro, Hitoshi; Kim, Sun-Jae; Passerini, Stefano; Sun, Yang-Kook; Myung, Seung-Taek</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">NPG Asia Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">e270</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NAMPCE</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1884-4057</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In the search for high-capacity anode materials, a facile hydrothermal route has been developed to synthesize phase-pure NiC2O4·2H2O nanorods, which were crystd. into the orthorhombic structure without using templates.  To ensure the elec. cond. of the nanorods, the produced NiC2O4·2H2O nanorods were attached to reduced graphene oxide (rGO) sheets via self-assembly layer-by-layer processes that utilize the electrostatic adsorption that occurs in a poly(diallyldimethylammonium chloride) soln.  The high elec. cond. aided by the presence of rGO significantly improved the electrochem. properties: 933 mAh g-1 for the charge capacity (oxidn.), which showed 87.5% efficiency at the first cycle with a retention of approx. 85% for 100 cycles, and 586 mAh g-1 at 10 C-rates (10 A g-1) for the NiC2O4·2H2O/rGO electrode.  The lithium storage processes were involved in the conversion reaction, which were fairly reversible via a transformation to Ni metal accompanied by the formation of a lithium oxalate compd. upon discharge (redn.) and restoration to the original NiC2O4·2H2O upon charging (oxidn.); this was confirmed via X-ray diffraction, transmission electron microscopy, X-ray photoelectron microscopy and time-of-flight secondary ion mass spectroscopy.  We believe that the high rate capacity and rechargeability upon cycling are the result of the unique features of the highly cryst. NiC2O4·2H2O nanorods assisted by conducting rGOs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrEuIq1hs3iC7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWfGFFp4RqCw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XotVyrtLs%253D&amp;md5=6941c2054f92d9611ecf4c1f6a01bcf7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.04.114"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Controlled synthesis of porous anhydrous cobalt oxalate nanorods with high reversible capacity and excellent cycling stability</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controlled synthesis of porous anhydrous cobalt oxalate nanorods with high reversible capacity and excellent cycling stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Junmin; He, Lei; Liu, Hui; Han, Tao; Wang, Yongjian; Zhang, Changjin; Zhang, Yuheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">One-dimensional porous anhyd. cobalt oxalate nanorods were prepd. via a facile water-controlled coppt. method followed by thermal annealing treatment under N2 at 300°.  The nanorods were characterized by using x-ray diffraction, SEM and TEM.     <span class="NLM_cas:volume">50</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4142-4148</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMTSAS</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A composite of transition metal oxide Co3O4 and multiwalled carbon nanotubes (MCNTs) was applied as an anode material for Na-ion batteries via a simply modified solid-state reaction and sonication method.  The as-prepd. Co3O4/MCNTs composite shows improved electrochem. performance than bare Co3O4 owing to the Co3O4/MCNTs nanostructure that benefits Na ion and electronic transport together with buffering the large vol. change of Co3O4 during charging and discharging process.  Addnl., the Na-storage behavior and the original capacity loss of Co3O4 based on the conversion reaction have been studied through cyclic voltammogram, x-ray diffraction, field-emission SEM, high-resoln. TEM, and selected area electron diffraction.  It is firstly demonstrated that in discharge state, Co3O4 particles initially react with Na to produce CoO and then is further reduced to nanosized Co in an amorphous Na oxides matrix.  In the charge process, Co nanoparticles were partially oxidized to Co3O4, the other part of the CoO remain leading capacity loss.  These results offer new insights into the electrochem. process of transition metal-based anode materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqtG50htnATz7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCDMmFcM9P9g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXltVWqt74%253D&amp;md5=afc7d19fa0d1cdc6653f1c05f8d44e80</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201002275"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Topochemical Synthesis of Cobalt Oxide-Based Porous Nanostructures for High-Performance Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Cheng Chao; Yin, Xiao Ming; Li, Qiu Hong; Chen, Li Bao; Wang, Tai Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two kinds of topochem. conversion routes from cobalt hydroxide precursors to cobalt oxide-based porous nanostructures are presented: pyrolysis in air and hydrothermal treatment by the Kirkendall diffusion effect.  These cobalt hydroxide precursors were synthesized by a simple hydrothermal approach with sodium acetate as mineralizer at 200°.  Detailed proof indicates that the process of cobalt hydroxide precursor growth is dominated by a nucleation, dissoln., renucleation, growth, and exfoliation mechanism.  By the topochem. conversion processes several Co3O4 nanostructures, such as cobalt oxide-coated cobalt hydroxide carbonate nanowires, cobalt oxide nanotubes, hollow cobalt oxide spheres, and porous cobalt oxide nanowires, have been synthesized.  The obtained Co3O4 nanostructures have also been evaluated as the anode materials in lithium-ion batteries.  It was found that the as-prepd. Co3O4 nanostructures exhibited high reversible capacity and good cycle performance due to their porous structure and small size.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrO2GMmK2HuRbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCDMmFcM9P9g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhtFKrur0%253D&amp;md5=f1e5d09d0139588b3367030ee6773eee</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201601357"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, W.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Understanding Origin of Voltage Hysteresis in Conversion Reaction for Na Rechargeable Batteries: The Case of Cobalt Oxides</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding Origin of Voltage Hysteresis in Conversion Reaction for Na Rechargeable Batteries: The Case of Cobalt Oxides</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Haegyeom; Kim, Hyunchul; Kim, Hyungsub; Kim, Jinsoo; Yoon, Gabin; Lim, Kyungmi; Yoon, Won-Sub; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">28</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Conversion reaction electrodes offer a high specific capacity in rechargeable batteries by utilizing wider valence states of transition metals than conventional intercalation-based electrodes and have thus been intensively studied in recent years as potential electrode materials for high-energy-d. rechargeable batteries.  However, several issues related to conversion reactions remain poorly understood, including the polarization or hysteresis during charge/discharge processes.  Herein, Co3O4 in Na cells is taken as an example to understand the aforementioned properties.  The large hysteresis in charge/discharge profiles is revealed to be due to different electrochem. reaction paths assocd. with resp. charge and discharge processes, which is attributed to the mobility gap among inter-diffusing species in a metal oxide compd. during de/sodiation.  Furthermore, a Co3O4-graphene nanoplatelet hybrid material is demonstrated to be a promising anode for Na rechargeable batteries, delivering a capacity of 756 mAh g-1 with a good reversibility and an energy d. of 96 Wh kg-1 (based on the total electrode wt.) when combined with a recently reported Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) cathode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqonCcTrGyWebVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCDMmFcM9P9g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xot1KhtbY%253D&amp;md5=2c733a2d989b088b081d8b9dcd0faaea</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.09.094"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Longoni, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fiore, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jung, Y.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Co3O4 negative electrode material for rechargeable sodium ion batteries: An investigation of conversion reaction mechanism and morphology-performances correlations</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Longoni, Gianluca; Fiore, Michele; Kim, Joo-Hyung; Jung, Young Hwa; Kim, Do Kyung; Mari, Claudio M.; Ruffo, Riccardo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal oxides have recently aroused a renewed and increasing interest as conversion anode materials for sodium ion batteries.  Being their electrochem. performances strongly dependent on morphol. aspects, has been here proposed a straightforward approach to modulate morphol. characteristics of a transition metal oxide (Co3O4) using a low cost synthetic route.  The as obtained optimized morphol. allows the realization of high practical specific capacities, higher than 500 mAh g-1 after 50 cycles, and represents a valid candidate for further optimization.  In addn. to the morphol.-performance correlations, the reaction mechanism beyond the electrochem. behavior was also investigated revealing the role of the CoO phase in the charge/discharge process.  Finally, an electrode pre-sodiation treatment for conversion materials is presented: it has been indeed demonstrated that it sensibly decreases the irreversible capacity correlated to the first cycle and improves cycle ability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq0FUraXWrcU7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCDMmFcM9P9g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFGqsbfI&amp;md5=11ca11bd9f23a5a42246eb5de6fa5a69</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1039/c5ee00695c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, C.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, J.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jung, H.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chung, K.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aurbach, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S.-T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NaCrO<sub>2</sub> cathode for high-rate sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insertion compounds and composites made by ball milling for advanced sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Biao; Dugas, Romain; Rousse, Gwenaelle; Rozier, Patrick; Abakumov, Artem M.; Tarascon, Jean-Marie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have been considered as potential candidates for stationary energy storage because of the low cost and wide availability of Na sources.  However, their future commercialization depends critically on control over the solid electrolyte interface formation, as well as the degree of sodiation at the pos. electrode.  Here we report an easily scalable ball milling approach, which relies on the use of metallic sodium, to prep. a variety of sodium-based alloys, insertion layered oxides and polyanionic compds. having sodium in excess such as the Na4V2(PO4)2F3 phase.  The practical benefits of prepg. sodium-enriched pos. electrodes as reservoirs to compensate for sodium loss during solid electrolyte interphase formation are demonstrated by assembling full C/P'2-Na1[Fe0.5Mn0.5]O2 and C/'Na3+xV2(PO4)2F3' sodium-ion cells that show substantial increases (&gt;10%) in energy storage d.  Our findings may offer electrode design principles for accelerating the development of the sodium-ion technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrdQwVANhMSw7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCDMmFcM9P9g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFOhsb8%253D&amp;md5=14b6f81901097d73e909b451e4a52b84</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1039/c5ra21235a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A type of sodium-ion full-cell with a layered NaNi<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode and a pre-sodiated hard carbon anode</span>. <i>RSC Adv.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">106519</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">106522</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c5ra21235a</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D106519-106522%26journal%3DRSC%2BAdv.%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BXiao%26author%3DC.%2BSun%26author%3DC.%2BLai%26author%3DX.%2BAi%26title%3DA%2Btype%2Bof%2Bsodium-ion%2Bfull-cell%2Bwith%2Ba%2Blayered%2BNaNi0.5Ti0.5O2%2Bcathode%2Band%2Ba%2Bpre-sodiated%2Bhard%2Bcarbon%2Banode%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc5ra21235a&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b13641&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc5ra21235a&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A type of sodium-ion full-cell with a layered NaNi0.5Ti0.5O2 cathode and a pre-sodiated hard carbon anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Hongbo; Xiao, Yazhou; Sun, Chuang; Lai, Chao; Ai, Xinping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">129</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">106519-106522</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">RSCACL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2046-2069</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new structure of sodium-ion full-cell with a layered NaNi0.5Ti0.5O2 cathode and a pre-sodiated hard carbon anode is reported.  The pre-sodiation of the hard carbon anode, achieved via a facile approach in a three-electrode battery, can significantly enhance the initial coulombic efficiency of the sodium-ion full-cell.  As a consequence, a much higher capacity is obtained in the hard carbon/NaNi0.5Ti0.5O2 sodium-ion battery.  Based on the cathode mass, the full-cell with the pre-sodiated hard carbon anode can exhibit a reversible capacity of 93 mA h g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr_2zWMBOTW5rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj559Jo7rIL7g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFWlu7rP&amp;md5=c164a42f421e9fbb6ae1ccf5d88b7dca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1021/nl500077v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oh, S.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, C.                 10.1021/nl500077v</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D14%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D1620-1626%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DS.-M.%2BOh%26author%3DS.-T.%2BMyung%26author%3DC.%2BS.%2BYoon%26author%3DJ.%2BLu%26author%3DJ.%2BHassoun%26author%3DB.%2BScrosati%26author%3DK.%2BAmine%26author%3DY.-K.%2BSun%26title%3DAdvanced%2BNa%255BNi0.25Fe0.5Mn0.25%255DO2%252FC-Fe3O4%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%2Busing%2BEMS%2Belectrolyte%2Bfor%2Benergy%2Bstorage%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fnl500077v&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b13641&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fnl500077v&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advanced Na[Ni0.25Fe0.5Mn0.25]O2/C-Fe3O4 Sodium-Ion Batteries Using EMS Electrolyte for Energy Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Oh, Seung-Min; Myung, Seung-Taek; Yoon, Chong Seung; Lu, Jun; Hassoun, Jusef; Scrosati, Bruno; Amine, Khalil; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1620-1626</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">While much research effort was devoted to the development of advanced Li-ion batteries for renewal energy storage applications, the Na-ion battery is also of considerable interest because Na is one of the most abundant elements in the Earth's crust.  The authors report a Na-ion battery based on a C-coated Fe3O4 anode, Na[Ni0.25Fe0.5Mn0.25]O2 layered cathode, and NaClO4 in fluoroethylene carbonate and Et methanesulfonate electrolyte.  This unique battery system combines an intercalation cathode and a conversion anode, resulting in high capacity, high rate capability, thermal stability, and much improved cycle life.  This performance suggests that the Na-ion system is potentially promising power sources for promoting the substantial use of low-cost energy storage systems in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrwahqJyE1xMbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj559Jo7rIL7g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXisFais74%253D&amp;md5=913ed26b737b8558b47cb94ad7248c22</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1039/c6ee00794e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An advanced high-energy sodium ion full battery based on nanostructured Na<sub>2</sub>Ti<sub>3</sub>O<sub>7</sub>/VOPO<sub>4</sub> layered materials</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3399</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3405</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c6ee00794e</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D9%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D3399-3405%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26author%3DL.%2BPeng%26author%3DY.%2BZhu%26author%3DD.%2BChen%26author%3DX.%2BZhang%26author%3DG.%2BYu%26title%3DAn%2Badvanced%2Bhigh-energy%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bfull%2Bbattery%2Bbased%2Bon%2Bnanostructured%2BNa2Ti3O7%252FVOPO4%2Blayered%2Bmaterials%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc6ee00794e&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b13641&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc6ee00794e&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An advanced high-energy sodium ion full battery based on nanostructured Na2Ti3O7/VOPO4 layered materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Hongsen; Peng, Lele; Zhu, Yue; Chen, Dahong; Zhang, Xiaogang; Yu, Guihua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3399-3405</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In virtue of the abundant sodium resources, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered to be one of the promising alternatives to lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, current research concs. mostly on sodium ion half-cells, and the development of sodium ion full cells with high performance remains a crit. challenge.  Here we rationally designed a full sodium-ion battery based on nanostructured Na2Ti3O7 and VOPO4 materials as the anodes and cathodes, owing to their advantageous electrochem. features.  The full cell outputs one of the highest operating voltages close to 2.9 V and delivers a large reversible capacity of 114 mA h g-1 at a rate of 0.1C.  It also shows outstanding rate capability (∼74 mA h g-1 at 2C rate) and excellent cycling stability (92.4% capacity retention after 100 cycles).  A high energy d. of 220 W h kg-1 is achieved, which is comparable to the state-of-the-art LIBs.  Moreover, the temp.-dependent charge-discharge tests indicate excellent capacity retentions in a wide temp. range of -20 to 55 °C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoeiSHi_Z7ig7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj559Jo7rIL7g"> &gt;&gt;                         rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly ordered mesoporous NiO anode material for lithium ion batteries with an excellent electrochemical performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Hao; Wang, Guoxiu; Liu, Jian; Qiao, Shizhang; Ahn, Hyojun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, we have synthesized highly ordered mesoporous NiO materials by a nanocasting method using mesoporous silica KIT-6 as the hard templates.  Mesoporous NiO particles were characterized by small angle x-ray diffraction, nitrogen adsorption/desorption, and transmission electron microscopy.  The results demonstrated that the as-prepd. mesoporous NiO had an ordered Ia3d sym. mesostructure, with a high surface area of 96 m2/g.  Mesoporous NiO materials were tested as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, exhibiting much lower activation energy (20.75 kJ/mol) compared to the bulk NiO (45.02 kJ/mol).  We found that the mesoporous NiO electrode has higher lithium intercalation kinetics than its bulk counterpart.  The sp. capacity of mesoporous NiO after 50 cycles was 680 mA-h/g at 0.1C, which was much higher than that of the com. bulk NiO (188 mA-h/g).  Furthermore, at a high rate of 2C, the discharge capacity of mesoporous NiO was as high as 515 mA-h/g, demonstrating the potential to be used for high-power lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoDRdP-s0KSNLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhNk6eCmxlrMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhvFCitLg%253D&amp;md5=9112d5c9634b902b5e84d50777e426d6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201200320"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vu, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stein, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Porous Electrode Materials for Lithium-ion Batteries-How to prepare them and what makes them special</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1056</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1085</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Numerous benefits of porous electrode materials for lithium ion batteries (LIBs) have been demonstrated, including examples of higher rate capabilities, better cycle lives, and sometimes greater gravimetric capacities at a given rate compared to nonporous bulk materials.  These properties promise advantages of porous electrode materials for LIBs in elec. and hybrid elec. vehicles, portable electronic devices, and stationary elec. energy storage.  This review highlights methods of synthesizing porous electrode materials by templating and template-free methods and discusses how the structural features of porous electrodes influence their electrochem. properties.  A section on electrochem. properties of porous electrodes provides examples that illustrate the influence of pore and wall architecture and interconnectivity, surface area, particle morphol., and nanocomposite formation on the utilization of the electrode materials, specific capacities, rate capabilities, and structural stability during lithiation and delithiation processes.  Recent applications of porous solids as components for three-dimensionally interpenetrating battery architectures are also described.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrR3Y5G3fAhCLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhNk6eCmxlrMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsFags7rO&amp;md5=85d4c67c1d9ac4beee04147e773fef4e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201002724"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Takahashi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, C. S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Amine, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yashiro, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanostructured TiO<sub>2</sub> and its application in lithium-ion storage</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>21</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3231</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3241</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201002724</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured TiO2 and Its Application in Lithium-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Myung, Seung-Taek; Takahashi, Naohiro; Komaba, Shinichi; Yoon, Chong Seung; Sun, Yang-Kook; Amine, Khalil; Yashiro, Hitoshi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3231-3241</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Titania nanorods and nanowires are synthesized via a hydrothermal reaction of amorphous TiO2 in alk. NaOH, followed by ion exchange in HCl aq. soln., and dehydration at 400 °C.  Although the hydrothermal treatment produces three different particle morphologies depending on the reaction time (nanosheets, nanorods, and nanowires), the products exhibit the same crystal structure.  Ion exchange of Na2Ti3O7 in HCl aq. soln. brings about a phase change to H2Ti3O7, but there is no change in the particle morphol.  Dehydration of the nanostructured H2Ti3O7 leads to two types of crystal structure-anatase TiO2 for the nanorods, and TiO2-B for the nanowires-although no significant difference is found in the morphol. of the products even after dehydration.  The nanorods are 40-50 nm in length and 10 nm in diam., whereas the nanowires are several micrometers in length and tens to hundreds of nanometers in thickness.  In-situ X-ray diffraction revealed the formation of anatase TiO2 from the TiO2-B above 450 °C.  This finding implies that the phase transformation occurs rather slowly for the TiO2-B nanowires due to the larger particle size and higher crystallinity of H2Ti3O7.  Tests with Li-metal half cells indicated that the anatase TiO2 nanorods are more favorable for the storage and release of Li ions because of their greater surface area than the TiO2-B nanowires.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo21FeXjpt3c7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhNk6eCmxlrMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXosVSjsLo%253D&amp;md5=8d5a685ba9a0d344012332e56b49bbca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1039/c3ee41960f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kikuchi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are in the spotlight as viable alternatives to lithium-ion batteries in stationary storage and power grid applications.  Among possible anode materials, Sb is one of the interesting candidates due to a combination of battery-type potential plateaus in the charge-discharge profiles, high capacity (theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1), and demonstrated good cyclic stability.  The effect of Sb particle size (particularly at the nanoscale range) and the compn. of Sb-carbon composites on the electrode performance, stability, and charge storage mechanism is systematically evaluated here for the first time.  A range of Sb-carbon nanocomposites with varied Sb particle size (between 50 and ∼1 nm) are studied.  The control of the particle size is achieved via varying the carbon and Sb wt. ratio in the precursors.  The shape of charge-discharge profiles, hysteresis, and the difference in cyclic stabilities and rate performance are analyzed.  The nanocomposite with the smallest particle size (∼1 nm) and the largest carbon content provides the most stable cyclic behavior and a better rate capability but suffers from an increased hysteresis between charge and discharge curves.  In situ synchrotron X-ray diffraction expts. indicate that the storage mechanism in the Sb-carbon nanocomposites contg.                         rightTab-cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal hydrides: an innovative and challenging conversion reaction anode for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Aymard, Luc; Oumellal, Yassine; Bonnet, Jean-Pierre</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Beilstein Journal of Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1821-1839</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">BJNEAH</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Beilstein-Institut zur Foerderung der Chemischen Wissenschaften</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The state of the art of conversion reactions of metal hydrides (MH) with lithium is presented and discussed in this review with regard to the use of these hydrides as anode materials for lithium-ion batteries.  A focus on the gravimetric and volumetric storage capacities for different examples from binary, ternary and complex hydrides is presented, with a comparison between thermodn. prediction and exptl. results.  MgH2 constitutes one of the most attractive metal hydrides with a reversible capacity of 1480 mA·h·g-1 at a suitable potential (0.5 V vs Li+/Li0) and the lowest electrode polarization (&lt;0.2 V) for conversion materials.  Conversion process reaction mechanisms with lithium are subsequently detailed for MgH2, TiH2, complex hydrides Mg2MHx and other Mg-based hydrides.  The reversible conversion reaction mechanism of MgH2, which is lithium-controlled, can be extended to others hydrides as: MHx + xLi+ + xe- in equil. with M + xLiH.  Other reaction paths-involving solid solns., metastable distorted phases, and phases with low hydrogen content-were recently reported for TiH2 and Mg2FeH6, Mg2CoH5 and Mg2NiH4.  The importance of fundamental aspects to overcome technol. difficulties is discussed with a focus on conversion reaction limitations in the case of MgH2.  The influence of MgH2 particle size, mech. grinding, hydrogen sorption cycles, grinding with carbon, reactive milling under hydrogen, and metal and catalyst addn. to the MgH2/carbon composite on kinetics improvement and reversibility is presented.  Drastic technol. improvement in order to the enhance conversion process efficiencies is needed for practical applications.  The main goals are minimizing the impact of electrode vol. variation during lithium extn. and overcoming the poor electronic cond. of LiH.  To use polymer binders to improve the cycle life of the hydride-based electrode and to synthesize nanoscale composite hydride can be helpful to address these drawbacks.  The development of high-capacity hydride anodes should be inspired by the emergent nano-research prospects which share the knowledge of both hydrogen-storage and lithium-anode communities.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoD1b1a4IYmRbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhnBz6JO0_Agg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs12hsL7N&amp;md5=bce842656656b3d6436db93ba41e141d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1016/s0378-7753(96)02580-3"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Arai, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Okada, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sakurai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamaki, J.-i.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cathode performance and voltage estimation of metal trihalides</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Binder-free NiO@MnO2 core-shell structure was deposited on Ni foam used as electrode of supercapacitor.  The rod-like NiO core was prepd. by thermal decompn. of NiC2O4 synthesized by corrosion of Ni foam with oxalic acid under hydrothermal conditions.  Sphere-like MnO2 shell was deposited on the surface of NiO core through hydrothermal treatment with KMnO4 soln.  The structure, compn., morphol. evolution and surface chem. state of the NiO@MnO2 electrode were analyzed by XRD, SEM, energy dispersive X-ray (EDX), TEM and XPS.  The obtained NiO and NiO@MnO2 electrodes were directly used as electrodes of supercapacitor, and their electrochem. performances were tested with cyclic voltammograms, galvanostatic charge/discharge and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy.  The sphere-like MnO2 shell leads to an impressive enhancement of the performance including the areal capacitance (a.c.) and cycling stability, particular in the AC.  To be more specific, the NiO@MnO2 exhibits a high a.c. of 3.584 F/cm2 at a c.d. of 5 mA/cm2, which is much higher than that of NiO electrode whose a.c. is 1.483 F/cm2 at the same c.d., demonstrating the potential to use NiO@MnO2 electrode for supercapacitor.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The combination of high-capacity and long-term cyclability has always been regarded as the first priority for next generation anode materials in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  To meet these requirements, the Ag nanoparticle decorated mesoporous SnO2/NiO nanotube (m-SNT) anodes were synthesized via an electrospinning process, followed by fast ramping rate calcination and subsequent chem. redn. in this work.  The one-dimensional porous hollow structure effectively alleviates a large vol. expansion during cycling as well as provides a short lithium-ion diffusion length.  Furthermore, metallic nickel (Ni) nanoparticles converted from the NiO nanograins during the lithiation process reversibly decomp. Li2O during delithiation process, which significantly improves the reversible capacity of the m-SNT anodes.  In addn., Ag nanoparticles uniformly decorated on the m-SNT via a simple chem. redn. process significantly improve rate capability and also contribute to long-term cyclability.  The m-SNT@Ag anodes exhibited excellent cycling stability without obvious capacity fading after 500 cycles with a high capacity of 826 mAh g-1 at a high c.d. of 1000 mA g-1.  Furthermore, even at a very high c.d. of 5000 mA g-1, the charge-specific capacity remained as high as 721 mAh g-1, corresponding to 60% of its initial capacity at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpftCbU7va2ebVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhnBz6JO0_Agg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhvVymtbfO&amp;md5=3d47d11dd5fa00e0a6870f8bdd6de061</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref20" class="rightTabRefNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.07.077"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ru, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A novelporous coral-like Zn<sub>0.5</sub>Ni<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> as an anode material forlithium ion batteries with excellent rate performance</span>. <i>J.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">By reason of rich Na resources, Na-ion batteries have excited enormous consideration for use in the developing energy-storage stations.  And not surprisingly, the exploration of cost-effective anode materials for SIBs have been a conspicuous topic.  Herein, Fe trioxide embedded in the N-doped C matrix with strong O-bridge bonds is synthesized by using the Fe based metal org. framework as template.  The obtained composite delivers excellent electrochem. properties, such as specific capacity of 473.7 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  Besides, the reversible capacity still remains at 155.3 mA h g-1 at the high d. of 4000 mA g-1.  This remarkable Na-ion storage capability could be attributed to the incorporation of N atoms into C matrix and the strong chem. bonds between Fe trioxide and C matrix, which can restrain electrode pulverization and also retain an interparticle connection even after long cycling that could offer a good electronic conductive pathway.  This strategy for prepg. Fe trioxide possess strong interfacial interaction with N-doped C matrix can be applied to other metal phosphides and metal oxide materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqQaoRVH8x2t7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh4nA_UqE2ttQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtVOisbzL&amp;md5=b20ddce2adeb0d8949f01490b61e0e7c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1021/jz2012066"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Slater, M. We have synthesized amorphous titanium dioxide nanotube electrodes directly grown on current collectors without binders and additives to use as an anode for sodium-ion batteries. Herein, molybdenum phosphide (MoP) nanorods wrapped with thin carbon layer have been prepd. and applied as an anode for SIBs.  By utilizing in situ X-ray diffraction technol., a conversion-type mechanism of MoP anode has been disclosed.  This kind of MoP electrode exhibits extraordinary electrochem. properties, including excellent cycling performance with a discharge capacity of 398.4 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 800 cycles, and remarkable rate capabilities, which remain 104.5 mA g-1 at 1600 mA h g-1 even after 10,000 loops.  The distinguished performances stem from synergetic merits of the morphol., structure, and mechanism of MoP.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Currently, SnC2O4 is considered as one of the most promising anode materials for high-energy lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) because its charge capacity is higher than that of metal oxides.  Herein, a facile microwave-assisted solvothermal method was employed to obtain SnC2O4/GO composites within only 30 min, which is time-efficient.  The amt. of SnC2O4 was increased to 95.3 wt% to improve the capacity of the composite.  Pure SnC2O4 with a high sp. surface area of 19.6 m2 g-1 without any other tin compd. was used for fabrication.  The SnC2O4/GO composite exhibited excellent electrochem. performance, with reversible discharge/charge capacity of 657/659 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.2 A g-1.  Furthermore, at high current densities of 1.0 and 2.0 A g-1, the SnC2O4/GO composite anode exhibited high reversible discharge/charge capacities of 553/552 and 418/414 mA h g-1, resp., after 200 cycles at room temp.  These improvements were likely obtained because SnC2O4 was well composited with graphene, which not only offered rapid electron transfer but also released the tension produced by the volumetric effect during repeated lithiation/delithiation.  Cyclic voltammetry (CV) was also performed to further study the electrochem. reactions of SnC2O4/GO.  The facile microwave-assisted solvothermal method used herein is considered as a highly efficient method to fabricate metal oxalate/graphene composites for use as anode materials in LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrgjOvTLSYwtrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh4nA_UqE2ttQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXotlGkt70%253D&amp;md5=1d2cc81169e0ea29d548fc390e38c6f0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.03.087"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The shape-controlled synthesis and novel lithium storage mechanism of as-prepared CuC<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub>·xH<sub>2</sub>O nanostructures</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A composite of transition metal oxide Co3O4 and multiwalled carbon nanotubes (MCNTs) was applied as an anode material for Na-ion batteries via a simply modified solid-state reaction and sonication method.  The as-prepd. Co3O4/MCNTs composite shows improved electrochem. performance than bare Co3O4 owing to the Co3O4/MCNTs nanostructure that benefits Na ion and electronic transport together with buffering the large vol. change of Co3O4 during charging and discharging process.  Addnl., the Na-storage behavior and the original capacity loss of Co3O4 based on the conversion reaction have been studied through cyclic voltammogram, x-ray diffraction, field-emission SEM, high-resoln. TEM, and selected area electron diffraction.  It is firstly demonstrated that in discharge state, Co3O4 particles initially react with Na to produce CoO and then is further reduced to nanosized Co in an amorphous Na oxides matrix.  In the charge process, Co nanoparticles were partially oxidized to Co3O4, the other part of the CoO remain leading capacity loss.  These results offer new insights into the electrochem. process of transition metal-based anode materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqtG50htnATz7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYoMOm_QdXnw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXltVWqt74%253D&amp;md5=afc7d19fa0d1cdc6653f1c05f8d44e80</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201002275"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Conversion reaction electrodes offer a high specific capacity in rechargeable batteries by utilizing wider valence states of transition metals than conventional intercalation-based electrodes and have thus been intensively studied in recent years as potential electrode materials for high-energy-d. rechargeable batteries.  However, several issues related to conversion reactions remain poorly understood, including the polarization or hysteresis during charge/discharge processes.  Herein, Co3O4 in Na cells is taken as an example to understand the aforementioned properties.  The large hysteresis in charge/discharge profiles is revealed to be due to different electrochem. reaction paths assocd. with resp. charge and discharge processes, which is attributed to the mobility gap among inter-diffusing species in a metal oxide compd. during de/sodiation.  Furthermore, a Co3O4-graphene nanoplatelet hybrid material is demonstrated to be a promising anode for Na rechargeable batteries, delivering a capacity of 756 mAh g-1 with a good reversibility and an energy d. of 96 Wh kg-1 (based on the total electrode wt.) when combined with a recently reported Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) cathode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqonCcTrGyWebVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYoMOm_QdXnw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xot1KhtbY%253D&amp;md5=2c733a2d989b088b081d8b9dcd0faaea</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.09.094"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Longoni, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fiore, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jung, Y.                 10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.09.094</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Co3O4 negative electrode material for rechargeable sodium ion batteries: An investigation of conversion reaction mechanism and morphology-performances correlations</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Longoni, Gianluca; Fiore, Michele; Kim, Joo-Hyung; Jung, Young Hwa; Kim, Do Kyung; Mari, Claudio M.; Ruffo, Riccardo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
